## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical kinetics, focusing on modeling the instantaneous rate of concentration change for a reacting species over time. The relationship between dA_dt and A typically follows power-law or rational rate expressions derived from reaction mechanisms, while explicit dependence on t often arises from catalyst deactivation, diffusion limitations, or consecutive reaction pathways.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (reaction rate independent of concentration, typical of surface-saturated catalysis)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or isomerization processes)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (elementary bimolecular collision reactions)
- Empirical power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (fractional or non-integer reaction orders from complex mechanisms)
- Autocatalytic mechanism: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 - A) (reaction accelerated by product or intermediate accumulation)
- Time-modulated decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * t) (gradual rate reduction due to diffusion limits or catalyst aging)
- Precursor-driven production: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) - c2 * A (consecutive reaction where species is produced then consumed)
- Cooperative binding kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (1 + c2 * A**c1) (multi-site activation without full saturation)
- Periodically forced system: dA_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) * A (chemically driven reaction with oscillatory external forcing)
- Polynomial rate expansion: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (Taylor series approximation of complex mechanistic rate laws)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Equilibrium relaxation ŌåÆ Linear dependence on deviation from steady state: dA_dt ŌłØ c0 * (A - c1)
- Catalytic deactivation ŌåÆ Multiplicative time decay factor on concentration-dependent rate: dA_dt ŌłØ exp(c0 * t) * A**c1
- Diffusion-limited regime ŌåÆ Inverse square root time scaling combined with concentration: dA_dt ŌłØ c0 * A / sqrt(1 + c1 * t)
- Induction/autocatalysis phase ŌåÆ Negative quadratic term with positive linear term creates sigmoidal concentration buildup: dA_dt ŌłØ c0 * A * (c1 - A)
- Bistable reaction networks ŌåÆ Cubic polynomial in concentration indicating multiple kinetic attractors: dA_dt ŌłØ c0 * A * (A - c1) * (A - c2)
- Fractional reaction order ŌåÆ Non-integer exponent on concentration reflecting complex surface adsorption or chain mechanisms: dA_dt ŌłØ c0 * A**c1 where 0 < c1 < 1
- Consecutive reaction intermediate ŌåÆ Difference between decaying production source and linear consumption: dA_dt ŌłØ c0 * exp(c1 * t) - c2 * A
- Steady-state approximation ŌåÆ Rate expressed as ratio of polynomial production to consumption terms balancing out over time
